

================================================================================
DESCRIPTION — FULL DIRECTORY MAP: Planing/
Styde Forge — Blueprint & Plan Repository
================================================================================

This file maps and describes every folder, subfolder, and file in the Planing/
directory. Four major project phases live here: Dashboard_Phase0, v1.0_Phase1,
v2.0_Phase2, and v3.0_Phase0 — plus a standalone Top_20_Agents.md.

================================================================================
ROOT LEVEL
================================================================================

Top_20_Agents.md
  A ranking/catalog of the 20 most important AI agents in the Styde ecosystem.
  Describes each agent's role, capabilities, and integration points. Serves as
  a master directory for bot orchestration across Styde/Hund/Hermes.

================================================================================
DASHBOARD_PHASE0/
================================================================================
Purpose: Complete specification for the Styde Dashboard v0 — a desktop-native
control panel built with Tauri (Rust backend) + React frontend. This is the
Phase 0 scope: a working prototype with shell, chat, model provider system,
agent monitoring, benchmark panel, and data layer.

--- 00_Overview (3 files) ---

Application_Architecture.md
  Full architectural blueprint of the Dashboard. Defines the three-layer stack:
  Tauri/Rust system layer, React/TypeScript UI layer, and IPC bridge. Covers
  process lifecycle, window management, event bus architecture, and how the
  Hermes CLI bridge connects the dashboard to the underlying agent system.
  Includes data flow diagrams for chat messages, agent spawns, and system
  events.

DASHBOARD_INDEX.md
  Master navigation index for ALL Phase 0 documents. A table of contents
  mapping every specification file to its section (01-10). Includes a
  dependency graph showing which documents must be read in which order
  to understand the full system.

Dashboard_Vision.md
  The "why" document. Defines the product vision: a unified desktop command
  center for managing multi-agent AI workflows. Target users are developers
  running Hermes/Forge locally. Covers design philosophy (speed over
  features, keyboard-first, dark-mode native), success criteria for Phase 0,
  and the north-star UX principles.

--- 01_Application_Shell (4 files) ---

Lifecycle_Management.md
  How the Tauri application starts, runs, and shuts down. Specifies startup
  sequence (splash screen -> preload checks -> main window -> system tray),
  lifecycle hooks (on_ready, on_focus, on_blur, on_close), and the state
  machine that governs app states (Loading, Ready, Minimized, Quitting).
  Includes error recovery procedures for crash scenarios.

Process_Control.md
  Defines how the Dashboard manages child processes (Hermes CLI, Forge agents,
  local model servers). Specifies process pools, health check intervals,
  graceful shutdown with SIGTERM, and automatic restart policies. Includes
  the ProcessManager API specification.

System_Tray_Integration.md
  System tray icon behaviour: right-click menu (Show/Hide, Status, Quit),
  tooltip updates reflecting agent status, and OS-specific considerations
  (Windows notification area vs macOS menu bar). Defines the tray icon state
  set (idle, busy, error, updating).

Window_Management.md
  Window geometry, multi-monitor support, window state persistence (position,
  size, maximized), and the "compact mode" that collapses the dashboard to a
  minimal sidebar. Includes protocols for programmatic window manipulation
  via IPC.

--- 02_UI_UX (4 files) ---

Component_Library.md
  Exhaustive catalog of every UI component: buttons, inputs, cards, modals,
  dropdowns, toasts, tooltips, data tables, tabs, and the chat message
  component. Each entry defines props, states (default, hover, active,
  disabled, loading, error), and accessibility attributes. Built on a custom
  design system, not off-the-shelf.

Design_System.md
  The visual language: color palette (dark navy background #0F172A, accent
  cyan #06B6D4, semantic colors for success/error/warning), typography
  (Inter for UI, JetBrains Mono for code), spacing scale (4px base unit),
  elevation/shadows, border radius, and motion/animation principles.
  Defines the token system consumed by every component.

Layout_Design.md
  Page layout specifications: the three-column layout (sidebar | main content
  | detail panel), responsive breakpoints, and the layout grid system.
  Includes wireframe descriptions for every major view: Dashboard Home,
  Agent Monitor, Chat, Settings, and Benchmark panels.

Onboarding_Flow.md
  First-run experience: splash screen, initial configuration wizard (API
  keys, model provider setup, workspace path), tooltip tour, and template
  selection. Designed to get a new user from zero to a running agent in
  under 2 minutes.

--- 03_Agent_Monitor (3 files) ---

Agent_Detail_View.md
  The deep-dive view for a single agent: live log stream, current task status,
  resource usage (CPU, memory, token count), conversation history, and
  controls (pause, resume, kill, edit). Specifies the real-time update
  mechanism via WebSocket/EventSource.

Agent_Tracking.md
  The master agent registry: how agents are discovered, tracked, and listed.
  Defines the AgentRecord schema, filtering/sorting capabilities, and the
  connection to the Hermes CLI bridge for agent lifecycle events. Includes
  the agent list view UI spec (table with status badges, search, bulk
  actions).

Spawn_New_Agent.md
  The agent creation interface: a form/modal where users configure a new
  agent — select model provider, set system prompt, assign skills, choose
  toolsets, and define resource limits. Includes validation rules, template
  system for common agent configurations, and the IPC call to trigger spawn.

--- 04_Benchmark_Panel (3 files) ---

Performance_Metrics.md
  Real-time and historical performance KPIs: latency (p50/p95/p99), throughput
  (tokens/sec, tasks/min), error rates, and resource utilization. Specifies
  the metrics pipeline from agent -> storage -> dashboard visualization.
  Includes alert threshold configuration.

Quality_Benchmarks.md
  Offline evaluation benchmarks: accuracy scores, human evaluation ratings,
  consistency metrics, and task completion rates. Defines how benchmark runs
  are triggered, stored (benchmark_history table), and compared across model
  versions. Includes the leaderboard view.

Visualization_Strategy.md
  Charting approach: which chart types for which metrics (line charts for
  time-series, bar charts for comparisons, heatmaps for correlation),
  interactive filtering, time-range selection, and export (PNG/CSV). Based
  on Recharts library with custom theming.

--- 05_Chat_Interface (4 files) ---

Chat_Agent_Tools.md
  How tools appear in the chat interface: inline tool calls rendered as
  collapsible cards, tool result previews, tool confirmation dialogs for
  dangerous operations. Specifies the tool registry and how tools register
  their UI components.

Chat_Architecture.md
  The full chat system design: message model (roles, content, attachments,
  metadata), conversation threading, streaming token display, markdown
  rendering, code block syntax highlighting, and the WebSocket connection
  to the agent backend. Covers both single-turn and multi-turn sessions.

Chat_Persistence.md
  How conversations are saved and restored: local SQLite storage, session
  export/import (JSON/Markdown), search across conversation history, and
  auto-save behaviour. Defines the storage schema and retention policies.

Skill_Command_System.md
  Slash-command system within the chat (/help, /spawn, /benchmark, /config,
  etc.). Specifies command parsing, autocomplete, parameter validation, and
  how commands map to internal API calls. The extensibility model allows
  plugins to register their own commands.

--- 06_Model_Provider_System (5 files) ---

Built_In_Providers.md
  Specs for built-in model providers: OpenAI (GPT-4o, GPT-4-turbo), Anthropic
  (Claude 3 Opus/Sonnet/Haiku), Google (Gemini Pro/Ultra), Mistral, Groq,
  and Ollama (local). Each provider entry defines auth method, API endpoint,
  supported models, rate limits, and default configuration.

Custom_Provider_API.md
  How users add custom providers: the provider plugin interface, configuration
  schema, authentication methods (API key, OAuth, custom header), and the
  required endpoints. Includes a step-by-step guide for writing a custom
  provider plugin.

Local_Model_Support.md
  Running models locally via Ollama, llama.cpp, or vLLM. Specifies hardware
  requirements, model discovery (auto-scan local models), GPU acceleration
  detection, and the local inference server management (start/stop/health).

Provider_Architecture.md
  The abstract provider system design: Provider interface, ModelConfig schema,
  token counting, streaming support, error handling (rate limits, timeouts,
  authentication failures), and fallback chains. The architecture supports
  transparent switching between providers.

Provider_Configuration_UI.md
  UI for configuring providers: API key entry (masked), model selection
  dropdowns, parameter sliders (temperature, top_p, max_tokens), and a
  test-connection button. Settings are persisted in a local config file.

--- 07_System_Control (3 files) ---

Configuration_Panel.md
  The settings/config view: tabs for General (theme, language, autostart),
  Providers (model configuration), Agents (default settings, resource limits),
  Storage (paths, export), and Advanced (debug mode, log level, port config).
  Each section maps to a config file schema.

Health_Monitoring.md
  System health dashboard: CPU/memory/disk gauges, agent process status
  indicators, model endpoint reachability checks, and a system log stream.
  Includes automated health checks at configurable intervals and alert
  notifications (toast, tray balloon, log entry).

Start_Stop_Pipeline.md
  The safe startup and shutdown sequence for the entire agent pipeline:
  service dependency ordering, pre-flight checks, graceful degradation on
  partial failure, and the shutdown order to prevent data loss. Specifies
  the pipeline state machine.

--- 08_Data_Layer (3 files) ---

Hermes_CLI_Bridge.md
  The IPC bridge between the Dashboard UI and the Hermes CLI agent. Defines
  every command the dashboard can send (spawn agent, send message, list agents,
  run benchmark, get config) and the response format. Uses JSON-RPC over
  stdin/stdout with the running Hermes process.

Local_Storage.md
  Local storage architecture: SQLite database schema for conversations, agent
  records, benchmark results, and configuration. File storage for logs,
  checkpoints, and exports. Defines backup and migration strategies.

Real_Time_Updates.md
  How the dashboard stays in sync with running agents: WebSocket connections,
  event subscription model, event types (agent_message, agent_status_change,
  benchmark_complete, system_alert), and reconnection logic.

--- 09_Technical_Stack (3 files) ---

Auto_Update.md
  Update mechanism: Tauri updater integration, version manifest, update
  channel (stable/beta/dev), delta updates for bandwidth saving, and
  rollback capability. Defines the update flow: check -> download ->
  verify -> install -> restart.

Build_Pipeline.md
  CI/CD pipeline: GitHub Actions workflow for building the Tauri desktop
  app on Windows/macOS/Linux, running tests, code signing (Windows),
  notarization (macOS), and publishing to GitHub Releases. Specifies the
  build toolchain (Rust toolchain, Node.js, Tailwind).

Desktop_Framework_Choice.md
  Why Tauri was chosen over Electron: smaller binary size (5MB vs 150MB+),
  lower memory usage, Rust security, native file system access, and system
  tray support. Acknowledges trade-offs (no Chrome DevTools, smaller
  ecosystem) and mitigation strategies.

--- 10_Phase_Transition (1 file) ---

Phase0_to_Phase1.md
  Transition plan from Phase 0 (prototype) to Phase 1 (production). Lists
  what must be completed before Phase 1 begins, what carries over, and what
  gets rewritten. Includes migration checklist and architectural changes
  that Phase 1 introduces (multi-user support, cloud sync, plugin system).

================================================================================
V1.0_PHASE1/
================================================================================
Purpose: Phase 1 of the Styde Forge system. Moves from prototype to
production-grade agent orchestration framework. Introduces the actual "Forge"
— a core loop that spawns, evaluates, and improves AI agents autonomously.

--- 00_Implementation_Overview (3 files) ---

IMPLEMENTATION_ORDER.md
  The build sequence for Phase 1: Forge Core first (bootstrap, circuit breaker,
  core loop), then Forge Spawn (blueprint loading, delegation, RAG), eval
  pipeline, improvement loop, dashboard shell, chat, and integration. Each
  step has estimated effort, dependencies, and acceptance criteria.

PHASE0_GAP_ANALYSIS.md
  A frank assessment of what Phase 0 didn't deliver. Lists missing features,
  incomplete specs, architectural debt, and decisions that need revisiting.
  Each gap is rated by severity (blocker/major/minor) and linked to a Phase 1
  deliverable that addresses it.

PHASE1_SCOPE.md
  The formal scope document: what's in (Forge Core, Forge Spawn, Eval Pipeline,
  Improvement Loop, Dashboard Shell, Chat, Integration) and what's explicitly
  out (multi-user, cloud, plugin ecosystem — those are Phase 2). Defines the
  "definition of done" for Phase 1.

--- 01_Forge_Core (4 files) ---

Bootstrap_Scripts.md
  How the Forge system initializes: environment checks (Python version, GPU
  availability, disk space), config loading, skill manifest loading, and
  dependency resolution. Includes the bootstrap sequence diagram and the
  script entry points (forge bootstrap, forge doctor).

Caveman_Ultra_Activation.md
  The "Caveman Ultra" mode — an ultra-compressed communication protocol for
  agent-to-agent messaging. Designed to minimize token usage (target ~75%
  reduction) by stripping all natural language fluff and using structured
  shorthand. Specifies the activation conditions, compression rules, and
  decompression layer.

Circuit_Breaker_Implementation.md
  Fault tolerance: circuit breaker pattern for API calls and agent operations.
  Three states: Closed (normal), Open (failing — fast-fail), Half-Open
  (testing recovery). Specifies thresholds (error count, time window), cooldown
  periods, and the implementation as a Python decorator/context manager.

Core_Loop_Implementation.md
  The heart of Forge: the main loop that orchestrates agent lifecycle.
  Pseudocode-level specification of the loop: 1) Load blueprint, 2) Spawn
  agent, 3) Monitor execution, 4) Evaluate output, 5) Improve blueprint,
  6) Loop or exit. Includes state management, error handling, and timeout
  logic.

--- 02_Forge_Spawn (3 files) ---

Blueprint_Loading_System.md
  How Forge loads agent blueprints from disk: YAML/JSON blueprint parsing,
  schema validation, dependency resolution (blueprint inheritance), and the
  blueprint cache. Defines the Blueprint schema (name, model, prompt, skills,
  tools, constraints, eval criteria).

Delegate_Task_Integration.md
  Integration with Hermes's delegate_task system: how Forge passes tasks to
  sub-agents, monitors completion, and collects results. Specifies the
  delegation API, timeout handling, and result aggregation.

RAG_Context_Injection.md
  How blueprints inject context from a knowledge base: chunking strategy,
  embedding model (text-embedding-3-small), vector store (Chroma/FAISS),
  retrieval parameters (top-k, similarity threshold), and context window
  management. Builds a persistent knowledge base from past agent runs.

--- 03_Forge_Eval (2 files) ---

Eval_Pipeline_Implementation.md
  The evaluation pipeline that runs after each agent execution: automated
  checks (schema validation, test pass/fail, performance metrics), LLM-as-judge
  scoring, and human review integration. Defines the EvalResult schema,
  scoring rubric, and pipeline stages.

Eval_Spec_Format.md
  The specification format for evaluation criteria: YAML-based eval specs
  with fields for name, description, eval_type (auto/llm/human), weight,
  pass_threshold, and parameters. Includes examples for common eval types
  (code quality, response accuracy, style compliance).

--- 04_Forge_Improve (3 files) ---

Blueprint_Improvement_Loop.md
  The improvement engine: takes eval results, identifies weaknesses, and
  generates blueprint modifications. Uses a feedback loop that compares
  expected vs actual outcomes, applies targeted improvements (prompt tuning,
  skill adjustments, constraint tightening), and re-runs the blueprint.

Skill_Extraction_System.md
  How Forge extracts reusable skills from successful agent runs: pattern
  detection, template generation, skill validation, and automatic registration
  in the skill catalog. The goal is to build an ever-growing library of
  proven agent capabilities.

Teacher_and_Persistence.md
  The "Teacher Agent" — a meta-agent that observes other agents, identifies
  learning opportunities, and stores insights in persistent memory. Covers
  the Teacher's knowledge base schema, observation model, and how lessons
  are applied to future blueprint executions.

--- 06_Dashboard_Shell (2 files) ---

Dashboard_Shell_Complete.md
  The Phase 1 dashboard: a complete rebuild based on Phase 0 learnings.
  Specifies the Tauri v2 setup, React 18 + TypeScript frontend, Rust backend
  commands, and the IPC protocol. Includes the full component tree and
  routing structure.

Tauri_Setup_and_Layout.md
  Step-by-step Tauri project setup: dependencies (tauri v2, @tauri-apps/api,
  react-router), folder structure, build configuration (tauri.conf.json),
  window configuration, and the initial layout with sidebar routing.

--- 07_Dashboard_Chat (1 file) ---

Provider_and_Chat_Implementation.md
  The chat system + model provider integration for Phase 1. Specifies the
  message loop, provider abstraction layer, streaming token display, tool
  call rendering, and conversation persistence. Builds on Phase 0's chat
  architecture with production-grade error handling and performance.

--- 08_Integration (3 files) ---

Forge_Dashboard_Bridge.md
  How the Forge backend communicates with the Dashboard frontend: IPC commands,
  event types, data serialization, and the bridge service layer. Defines every
  message type (forge:agent_spawned, forge:eval_complete, forge:improvement,
  forge:error) and their payload schemas.

P0_Exit_Criteria.md
  Criteria for exiting Phase 0 and beginning Phase 1 implementation. A
  checklist of must-have conditions: all specs reviewed, tech decisions made,
  toolchain ready, and team aligned. Used as the gate between planning and
  building.

Week_Execution_Plan.md
  The actual build schedule: a week-by-week plan for implementing Phase 1.
  Breaks the full scope into weekly sprints with specific deliverables, owner
  assignments, and review gates. Estimated at 8-10 weeks for a solo developer.

--- Root Level (2 files) ---

PHASE1_INDEX.md
  Master index for all Phase 1 documents. Table of contents with document
  descriptions, dependency links, and status indicators (draft/review/final).
  The entry point for anyone navigating Phase 1 documentation.

PHASE1_ROADMAP.md
  High-level roadmap: Phase 1 milestones, timeline (Q2-Q3 2025), key
  deliverables, risk factors, and success metrics. Gives executive summary
  of the Phase 1 journey.

================================================================================
V2.0_PHASE2/
================================================================================
Purpose: Phase 2 of Styde Forge — advanced capabilities built on Phase 1's
foundation. Introduces Bayesian optimization, multi-judge evaluation, learning
systems, resource management, multi-agent orchestration, automation, and a
mature dashboard with Phase 1 & 2 features.

--- 00_Overview (3 files) ---

IMPLEMENTATION_ORDER.md
  Phase 2 build order: Bayesian Optimization first (foundation for intelligent
  tuning), then Multi-Judge Eval (better evaluation), Learning Systems
  (self-improvement), Resource Management (efficiency), Multi-Agent (scale),
  Automation (autonomy), Dashboard P1P2 (unified UI), and Integration (glue).

PHASE1_TO_PHASE2_TRANSITION.md
  What changes between Phase 1 and 2: architectural additions, new dependencies,
  breaking changes to Phase 1 APIs, migration strategies, and what gets
  deprecated. Ensures a smooth upgrade path from P1 to P2.

PHASE2_SCOPE.md
  Scope document: what's in (Bayesian optimization, multi-judge, learning
  systems, resource governor, multi-agent orchestration, automation engine,
  unified dashboard) and what's out (Phase 3 items like distributed execution,
  federated learning, marketplace).

--- 01_Bayesian_Optimization (1 file) ---

README.md
  Specification for the Bayesian optimization module. Uses Gaussian Process
  regression to optimize model parameters (temperature, top_p, frequency
  penalty, presence penalty) based on evaluation scores. Defines the
  acquisition function (Expected Improvement), parameter search space,
  and integration with the eval pipeline.

--- 02_Multi_Judge_Eval (1 file) ---

README.md
  Multi-judge evaluation system: runs the same output through multiple LLM
  judges (different models/prompts), aggregates scores using weighted voting
  or consensus algorithms, and produces a calibrated final score. Reduces
  individual judge bias and improves evaluation reliability.

--- 03_Learning_Systems (1 file) ---

README.md
  Meta-learning module: tracks patterns across all agent runs, identifies
  what works (success patterns) and what doesn't (failure modes), and
  automatically updates blueprints and skills. Implements few-shot learning
  from execution history and task clustering for transfer learning.

--- 04_Resource_Management (1 file) ---

README.md
  Resource governor: monitors and limits CPU, memory, GPU, and token usage
  across all running agents. Implements fair scheduling, priority queues,
  resource quotas per agent/workspace, and automatic scaling (spin down
  idle agents, throttle greedy ones). Includes cost tracking per model
  provider.

--- 05_Multi_Agent (1 file) ---

README.md
  Multi-agent orchestration: coordinates multiple agents working on the same
  or related tasks. Specifies communication protocols (agent-to-agent message
  passing), task decomposition (break task into sub-tasks for parallel agents),
  conflict resolution (when agents disagree), and consensus mechanisms.

--- 06_Automation (1 file) ---

README.md
  The automation engine: cron-job style scheduling for agent tasks, event-driven
  triggers (file change, webhook, time), pipeline composition (chain agents
  into workflows), and self-healing (retry failed tasks, alert on persistent
  failure). Users can set up recurring agent runs without manual intervention.

--- 07_Dashboard_P1P2 (1 file) ---

README.md
  The unified dashboard covering both Phase 1 (core monitoring) and Phase 2
  (advanced analytics). New views: optimization dashboard (Bayesian progress),
  evaluation leaderboard (multi-judge scores), learning dashboard (skill
  growth, pattern discovery), and resource dashboard (usage, costs, limits).
  All views share the Phase 1 shell and design system.

--- 08_Integration (1 file) ---

Week_Execution_Plan.md
  Phase 2 build schedule: week-by-week sprints for 12-14 weeks. Each week
  has specific deliverables from the scope areas, testing requirements, and
  integration checkpoints. Designed for a solo developer or small team.

--- Root Level (1 file) ---

PHASE2_INDEX.md
  Master document index for Phase 2 with links, statuses, and prerequisites.

================================================================================
V3.0_PHASE0/
================================================================================
Purpose: The most comprehensive phase — Phase 3 / v3.0 Phase 0. This is an
ambitious redesign of the entire Forge system with deep technical sophistication.
Adds Bayesian sampling (HMC, NUTS), formal state machines, hardware adaptation
layer, advanced eval pipelines, meta-learning, persistence safety, multi-agent
security, import/export, risk management, operations infrastructure, knowledge
management, teacher agents, hooks/events systems, and RAG retrieval.

--- 00_Overview (13 files) ---

00_Glossary.md
  Comprehensive glossary of every technical term used across v3.0. Defines
  ~200+ terms spanning Bayesian statistics, ML evaluation, agent architectures,
  sampling methods, and system design. Serves as the canonical reference for
  terminology consistency.

Component_Interfaces.md
  Formal interface specifications for every major component in v3.0. Uses
  TypeScript-style type definitions to describe input/output contracts,
  error types, and lifecycle hooks. Covers ~30 component interfaces across
  all subsystems (Sampler, Evaluator, Governor, Teacher, etc.).

Config_Reference.md
  Complete configuration schema for v3.0: YAML structure, every parameter
  with type, default, range, and description. Organized by subsystem (core,
  eval, sampling, meta, persistence, operations). The definitive reference
  for configuring a v3.0 Forge instance.

Core_Loop_Detail.md
  Deep-dive into the v3.0 core loop: a sophisticated state machine with 12
  states (Idle, Loading, Spawning, Executing, Monitoring, Evaluating,
  Improving, Recording, Learning, Updating, Sleeping, Error). Each state
  has entry/exit actions, transitions, timeout behaviour, and error handling.

Data_Models.md
  All data models/schemas in v3.0: AgentRecord, Blueprint, EvalResult,
  MetricSample, Checkpoint, Skill, KnowledgeEntry, Task, Session. Each model
  is defined with fields, types, constraints, and relationships. The data
  dictionary for the entire system.

DECISIONS.md
  Architecture Decision Records (ADRs): every significant technical decision,
  the alternatives considered, the chosen approach, and the rationale. Covers
  ~40 decisions spanning sampling methods, storage engines, IPC protocols,
  and ML approaches. The institutional memory of why things are built the
  way they are.

Master_Architecture_Overview.md
  The top-level architecture document. One-page diagram (described in text)
  showing all subsystems and their connections: Forge Core, Eval Pipeline,
  Sampling Stack, Meta Layer, Hardware Layer, Multi-Agent, Knowledge
  Management, Operations, and Dashboard Bridge. Each subsystem gets a
  paragraph explaining its role.

PHASE0_INDEX.md
  Master index for v3.0 Phase 0 documents. Maps every document to its
  section and provides dependency ordering. The navigation entry point.

Phase0_to_Phase1_Transition.md
  Transition plan from v3.0 Phase 0 (this planning/design phase) to Phase 1
  (implementation). Lists exactly which documents become implementation
  tickets, which are reference-only, and the order of implementation. A
  bridge between planning and building.

State_Machines.md
  Formal state machine definitions for all stateful components: Core Loop
  (12 states), Agent Lifecycle (8 states), Pipeline (6 states), Hardware
  Manager (5 states), and Connection Manager (4 states). Each machine
  defines states, transitions, events, and guards.

System_Startup_Shutdown.md
  The system startup and shutdown sequence: ordered initialization across all
  subsystems, dependency resolution, health verification, graceful degradation,
  and the emergency shutdown procedure. Startup has 8 phases, shutdown has 6,
  each with timeout and error handling.

Testing_Strategy.md
  Comprehensive testing strategy: unit tests (pytest, 90%+ coverage),
  integration tests (subsystem interaction), end-to-end tests (full pipeline
  runs), performance benchmarks (latency, throughput, memory), and chaos
  testing (fault injection, recovery verification). Specifies test
  infrastructure and CI integration.

USB_Directory_Structure.md
  The directory layout for the Forge system on a USB drive/USB stick — the
  entire system is designed to be portable from a USB drive. Defines the
  folder hierarchy, naming conventions, and which directories are synced
  vs local-only.

--- 01_Vision (2 files) ---

Blueprint_Catalog.md
  A catalog of ready-to-use agent blueprints shipped with v3.0. Each entry:
  name, description, model recommendation, skill requirements, estimated
  cost per run, and typical use case. Covers ~25 blueprints across categories
  (coding, research, analysis, creative, ops).

Vision_and_Goals.md
  The v3.0 vision statement: "An autonomous AI development forge that designs,
  builds, evaluates, and improves its own agents." Goals include full
  autonomy (human-in-the-loop only for critical decisions), self-optimization
  (Bayesian tuning of every parameter), and portability (runs from USB with
  zero installation).

--- 02_Hardware (2 files) ---

Hardware_Adaptation_Layer.md
  Abstract hardware layer that adapts Forge to any hardware: detects GPU
  (NVIDIA CUDA, AMD ROCm, Apple Metal), CPU cores, RAM, and disk speed.
  Auto-configures model sizes, batch sizes, and parallelism based on
  available hardware. Supports headless/server environments without display.

Resource_Governor.md
  Advanced resource management: soft/hard limits per agent, dynamic
  allocation based on priority, GPU memory partitioning, token budgets
  (daily/weekly), cost-aware scheduling (cheapest model for easy tasks),
  and proactive scaling (predict demand from history).

--- 03_Eval_Pipeline (6 files) ---

Automatic_Validation.md
  Automated validation rules for agent outputs: schema validation (JSON
  Schema), constraint satisfaction (logical rules), consistency checks
  (cross-reference with known facts), and output format verification.
  Runs before LLM-based evaluation to catch obvious issues early.

Bayesian_Weight_Optimization.md
  Bayesian optimization applied to evaluation weights: treats each evaluation
  criterion's weight as a hyperparameter, uses Gaussian Process regression
  to find the weight combination that best predicts human judgment. Closes
  the loop between automated and human evaluation.

Benchmark_Catalog.md
  Catalog of built-in benchmarks: coding benchmarks (HumanEval, MBPP),
  reasoning (GSM8K, MATH), language (MMLU, HellaSwag), and custom
  (Styde-specific task suites). Each benchmark entry defines the dataset,
  evaluation protocol, scoring system, and reference performance.

Bias_Calibration.md
  Bias detection and calibration in LLM judges: identifies systematic biases
  (verbosity preference, position bias, self-enhancement bias), measures
  bias magnitude, and applies calibration corrections. Includes a built-in
  bias audit tool that runs periodically.

Cross_Judge_Consensus.md
  Consensus algorithms for multi-judge evaluation: majority voting, weighted
  voting (by historical accuracy), Bayesian aggregation, and confidence-based
  filtering. Specifies when each algorithm is appropriate and how to handle
  judge disagreement.

LLM_as_Judge.md
  LLM-as-judge methodology: judge prompt templates, evaluation rubrics,
  scoring scales (numeric, Likert, pass/fail), reference-based vs reference-free
  evaluation, and chain-of-thought judging. Includes templates for common
  evaluation scenarios (code quality, response helpfulness, factual accuracy,
  style compliance).

Self_Evaluation_System.md
  The system by which Forge evaluates its own performance: meta-evaluation
  (how good is our evaluation?), drift detection (is evaluation quality
  declining over time?), and automatic recalibration when drift is detected.
  The "watching the watchers" layer.

--- 04_Sampling_Stack (5 files) ---

Dual_Averaging.md
  Dual averaging algorithm for adaptive step size in MCMC sampling. Used to
  automatically tune the step size parameter in HMC/NUTS. Full mathematical
  specification: target acceptance rate, iteration schedule, and parameter
  update rules.

Hamiltonian_Monte_Carlo.md
  HMC specification: the physics-inspired MCMC method that uses gradient
  information to propose efficient moves through parameter space. Defines
  the leapfrog integrator, potential/kinetic energy functions, and the
  Metropolis acceptance step. Used for Bayesian optimization of model
  parameters.

NUTS_Algorithm.md
  The No-U-Turn Sampler: an extension of HMC that automatically determines
  the optimal trajectory length (eliminating the need to manually set
  path length). Specifies the doubling procedure, slice variable, and
  U-turn detection criterion. The primary sampler for v3.0 optimization.

Tree_Depth_Optimization.md
  NUTS tree depth management: adaptive tree depth based on parameter
  geometry, max_tree_depth configuration, and the trade-off between
  exploration quality and computational cost. Includes strategies for
  high-dimensional parameter spaces.

Variational_Inference.md
  Variational inference as a faster alternative to MCMC: mean-field VI,
  automatic differentiation variational inference (ADVI), and the
  evidence lower bound (ELBO). Used for quick approximate posterior
  estimates when full MCMC is too expensive. Specifies when to use VI
  vs HMC vs NUTS.

--- 05_Meta_Layer (4 files) ---

Automatic_Version_Increment.md
  Semantic versioning system for blueprints and skills: automatic version
  bumps based on change type (patch/minor/major), changelog generation,
  and version compatibility checking. Blueprint evolution is tracked
  like software versioning.

Dynamic_Model_Selector.md
  Intelligent model selection: based on task type, complexity, token budget,
  and latency requirements, automatically selects the optimal model from
  available providers. Uses a cost-benefit analysis (capability score per
  token cost) to make the choice. Overridable by the user.

Historical_Learning_System.md
  Long-term learning: aggregates results across all runs, identifies
  performance trends, stores "lessons learned" in a structured knowledge
  base, and applies them to future runs. Implements a feedback delay
  mechanism to avoid recency bias in learning.

Self_Monitoring_Health.md
  Health monitoring of Forge itself: internal metrics (loop iteration time,
  memory usage, error frequency), anomaly detection, automatic health
  reports, and self-healing actions (restart stalled components, clear
  stuck queues, recover from OOM). The system watches itself.

--- 06_Persistence_Safety (4 files) ---

Atomic_Checkpoint_Writes.md
  Atomic write operations for checkpoints: uses temporary files + rename
  to ensure checkpoints are never corrupted by partial writes. Specifies
  the checkpoint format, write frequency, and recovery procedure.

Automatic_Recovery.md
  Recovery from crashes and power loss: startup integrity check, detect
  incomplete operations, roll back partial writes, and resume from last
  valid checkpoint. Ensures the system never loses data even on hard crash.

Filesystem_Transactions.md
  Transactional filesystem operations: all-or-nothing file operations
  (create blueprint, save eval result, update config). Uses a write-ahead
  log (WAL) pattern. If any step in a transaction fails, the entire
  operation rolls back.

Risk_Register.md
  Formal risk register: identifies every risk to data integrity and system
  availability, rates each by probability/impact, and documents mitigations.
  Covers ~25 risks across categories (hardware failure, software bugs,
  user error, external API failures, security incidents).

--- 07_Multi_Agent (2 files) ---

Multi_Agent_Collaboration.md
  Advanced multi-agent collaboration: agent roles (leader, worker, critic,
  observer), communication protocols (direct message, broadcast, shared
  blackboard), conflict resolution, voting mechanisms, and task allocation
  algorithms. Designed for teams of 2-20 agents working on complex goals.

Security_Model.md
  Security architecture: agent identity and authentication, action permission
  scoping, sandboxing (restricted filesystem/network access per agent),
  audit logging of all agent actions, and the "human-in-the-loop" gates
  for high-risk operations. Prevents one compromised agent from harming
  the system.

--- 08_Import_Export (2 files) ---

Import_Strategy.md
  How Forge imports external blueprints, skills, and configurations:
  format support (YAML, JSON, TOML), schema validation on import,
  dependency resolution, and conflict handling (version clashes, name
  collisions). Supports importing from GitHub repos, local files, and
  the community registry.

Sync_Strategy.md
  Sync strategy between Forge instances: two-way sync of blueprints,
  skills, knowledge base, and configuration. Uses a CRDT-inspired approach
  for conflict resolution. Supports sync over LAN, USB drive sneakernet,
  and cloud storage (S3, Google Drive, Dropbox).

--- 09_Risk_Maintenance (1 file) ---

Maintenance_Cleanup_Strategy.md
  Proactive maintenance: log rotation, checkpoint pruning (keep last N),
  database vacuuming, temporary file cleanup, and skill/blueprint
  deduplication. Runs on a schedule (weekly full, daily quick) and
  alerts the user if cleanup reclaims significant space.

--- 10_Operations (7 files) ---

API_Key_Management.md
  Secure API key storage: encrypted config file (AES-256-GCM), keyring
  integration (Windows Credential Manager, macOS Keychain), environment
  variable fallback, and key rotation procedures. Never stores keys in
  plaintext. Includes an audit log of key usage.

Blueprint_Validation.md
  Blueprint validation rules: schema conformance, model availability check,
  resource requirement check, skill dependency resolution, and test
  execution. Runs before any blueprint is loaded for execution. Provides
  detailed error messages for validation failures.

Caveman_Ultra_Mode.md
  Activation and deactivation protocol for Caveman Ultra mode. Defines the
  trigger conditions (token budget below threshold, manual activation,
  priority mode), the compression ratio targets, and the reversion
  conditions. Complete specification of the Caveman Ultra language.

Cost_Token_Tracking.md
  Cost and token tracking: per-agent, per-session, per-day, and per-month
  token usage. Cost calculation based on provider pricing. Visualized in
  the dashboard as charts and budgets. Supports budget alerts (notify when
  approaching limit) and hard caps (stop when limit reached).

Human_Oversight_Points.md
  Where humans must be in the loop: high-cost operations (over budget
  threshold), destructive actions (delete, reset, modify system files),
  model deployment to production, and security-sensitive operations.
  Each oversight point defines the required approval flow and fallback
  behaviour if human is unreachable.

Logging_Strategy.md
  Comprehensive logging: structured JSON logs, log levels (debug, info,
  warn, error, fatal), log rotation (size-based, 100MB per file, keep 10),
  log categories (system, agent, eval, meta, security), and log shipping
  (local file, optional remote syslog). Includes PII redaction in logs.

Skill_Loading_Mechanism.md
  Skill discovery and loading: scans skill directories, validates skill
  manifests, resolves inter-skill dependencies, and loads them into the
  agent context. Supports both built-in skills and user-authored skills.
  Defines the skill manifest schema and loading priority.

--- 11_Knowledge_Management (1 file) ---

Knowledge_Management.md
  Knowledge management system: how Forge stores, indexes, retrieves, and
  updates knowledge. Uses a hybrid approach (vector embeddings for semantic
  search, graph database for relationships, document store for raw content).
  Supports automated knowledge extraction from agent conversations and
  manual knowledge entry.

--- 12_Teacher_Agent (1 file) ---

Teacher_Agent.md
  The Teacher Agent specification: a meta-agent that observes all other
  agents, analyzes their successes and failures, extracts patterns, and
  generates lessons. Lessons are stored in the knowledge base and used
  to improve future blueprints. The Teacher operates continuously in
  the background with minimal resource footprint.

--- 13_Hooks_Events (1 file) ---

Hooks_Events.md
  Event system and hook architecture: event bus (publish/subscribe), event
  types (pre/post execution, state change, error, metric), hook registration
  API, and the lifecycle hook system (before_agent_spawn, after_eval,
  on_error, etc.). Enables plugins and custom integrations to extend Forge
  without modifying core code.

--- 14_RAG_Retrieval (1 file) ---

RAG_Retrieval.md
  Retrieval-Augmented Generation system: document ingestion pipeline (chunk,
  embed, index), retrieval strategies (semantic search, keyword hybrid,
  contextual retrieval), context assembly (reranking, deduplication, window
  expansion), and integration with agent prompts. The knowledge foundation
  for informed agent decisions.

--- Root Level (1 file) ---

PHASE0_COMPLETE.md
  Declaration that v3.0 Phase 0 (the planning and design phase) is complete.
  Contains a checklist of every document in the phase, its review status,
  and the official sign-off. Marks the transition eligibility to Phase 1
  implementation.

dashboard prototype through three major iterations, culminating in a
sophisticated autonomous AI development forge with Bayesian optimization,
multi-agent orchestration, self-evaluation, and portable USB operation.

# Application Architecture

**StydeForge Dashboard — Mission Control**
**Phase 0 Design Document**

---

## 1. Architecture Overview

```
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    StydeForge.exe                        │
│                   (Desktop Application)                   │
│                                                          │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │                  UI Layer (HTML/CSS/JS)             │  │
│  │  ┌───────────┐  ┌────────────┐  ┌───────────────┐  │  │
│  │  │  Agents   │  │ Benchmarks │  │    Chat       │  │  │
│  │  │  Panel    │  │   Panel    │  │    Panel      │  │  │
│  │  └─────┬─────┘  └─────┬──────┘  └───────┬───────┘  │  │
│  └────────┼──────────────┼─────────────────┼──────────┘  │
│           │              │                 │              │
│  ┌────────┴──────────────┴─────────────────┴──────────┐  │
│  │                Core Controller                      │  │
│  │  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────────────┐  │  │
│  │  │Process   │  │Benchmark │  │ Chat Controller  │  │  │
│  │  │Manager   │  │Engine    │  │                  │  │  │
│  │  └────┬─────┘  └────┬─────┘  └────────┬─────────┘  │  │
│  └───────┼─────────────┼────────────────┼────────────┘  │
│          │             │                │                │
│  ┌───────┴─────────────┴────────────────┴────────────┐  │
│  │                  Data Layer                        │  │
│  │  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────┐  ┌──────────────────┐ │  │
│  │  │ Hermes   │  │ Local DB │  │ Provider API     │ │  │
│  │  │ CLI      │  │(IndexedDB│  │ Layer            │ │  │
│  │  │ Bridge   │  │ /SQLite) │  │                  │ │  │
│  │  └──────────┘  └──────────┘  └──────────────────┘ │  │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
│                                                          │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │              Desktop Shell (Tauri)                  │  │
│  │  • Window management    • System tray              │  │
│  │  • Native file dialogs  • Auto-start               │  │
│  │  • Process spawning     • File system access       │  │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
         │                 │                  │
         ▼                 ▼                  ▼
┌──────────────┐  ┌──────────────┐  ┌──────────────────┐
│ Hermes CLI   │  │ File System  │  │ AI Provider APIs │
│ (hermes ...) │  │ (D:/, /logs) │  │ (DeepSeek,       │
│              │  │              │  │  OpenAI, Custom)  │
└──────────────┘  └──────────────┘  └──────────────────┘
```

---

## 2. Layers

### 2.1 Desktop Shell (Tauri)

Responsibilities:
- Create the application window
- System tray integration (minimize, notifications)
- Start/stop Hermes as child process
- Native features: filesystem, file dialogs, auto-start
- Low resource usage (Rust backend, ~5-10MB)

### 2.2 UI Layer (HTML/CSS/JS)

Three main panels in a responsive grid:
- **Agent Panel** (left 30%) — agent list, status, details
- **Benchmark Panel** (center/right 35%) — graphs, performance data
- **Chat Panel** (right/bottom 35%) — chat with full agent

### 2.3 Core Controller

Business logic:
- **Process Manager** — polls Hermes CLI, keeps agent list synchronized
- **Benchmark Engine** — collects performance data, computes graphs
- **Chat Controller** — manages provider selection, tool calls, streaming

### 2.4 Data Layer

- **Hermes CLI Bridge** — calls `hermes process list`, `hermes cronjob list`, etc.
- **Local DB** — stores history (agent history, chat logs, benchmarks)
- **Provider API Layer** — abstract interface to AI models

---

## 3. Tech Stack (preliminary)

| Layer | Technology | Rationale |
|-------|-----------|-----------|
| Desktop Shell | **Tauri v2** (Rust) | Small .exe (~5MB), native performance, memory efficient |
| UI Rendering | HTML/CSS/JS via Tauri WebView | Full flexibility, easy styling |
| Charts | Chart.js (lightweight) | Good performance, dark theme support |
| Chat Rendering | Markdown + syntax highlighting | Code blocks, tables, formatting |
| Local DB | IndexedDB (MVP) → SQLite (Phase 2) | No server dependencies |
| Process Communication | Tauri Command API (Rust ↔ JS) | Safe IPC, typed |
| Build System | Tauri CLI + GitHub Actions | Build .exe for Windows |

---

## 4. Communication Flows

### 4.1 Agent Monitoring

```
UI ──→ Core Controller ──→ Hermes CLI Bridge ──→ hermes process list
                                                      │
UI ←── Core Controller ←── Hermes CLI Bridge ←───────┘
(polls every 2 seconds)
```

### 4.2 Chat with Tools

```
User: "read D:/config.yaml"
        │
Chat Controller:
  1. Send to chosen AI Provider (DeepSeek/OpenAI/etc.)
     with tool definitions
  2. Provider responds: tool_call: read_file("D:/config.yaml")
  3. Chat Controller executes via Tauri filesystem API
  4. Result sent back to provider
  5. Provider formulates response
  6. Streamed to UI (markdown)
```

### 4.3 System Control

```
UI [▶ Start] ──→ Core Controller ──→ Tauri spawn process
                                        │
                              ┌─────────┴──────────┐
                              │ Hermes process     │
                              │ (Forge loop)       │
                              └────────────────────┘

UI [⏹ Stop] ──→ Core Controller ──→ kill process
                              ┌─────────┴──────────┐
                              │ Graceful shutdown  │
                              │ → save checkpoints │
                              │ → stop cron jobs   │
                              └────────────────────┘
```

---

## 5. Security Model

| Feature | Risk | Mitigation |
|---------|------|------------|
| Chat runs terminal commands | Malicious commands | Confirmation dialog for all commands, sandbox mode |
| Chat writes files | Overwrites important files | Show diff before write, `--dry-run` first |
| Chat reads files | Reads sensitive data | No mitigation — user's responsibility (local app) |
| Custom providers | API keys stored | Encrypted local storage (OS keychain) |

---

## 6. Configuration

`StydeForge.exe` reads config from:
```
%APPDATA%/StydeForge/config.json
```

```json
{
  "version": "1.0",
  "hermes_path": "C:/Users/Pontus/.hermes",
  "providers": {
    "deepseek": {
      "api_key": "sk-...",
      "default_model": "deepseek-v4-pro"
    },
    "openai": {
      "api_key": "sk-...",
      "default_model": "gpt-4o"
    }
  },
  "appearance": {
    "font_size": 14,
    "font": "JetBrains Mono",
    "default_layout": "3-panels"
  },
  "chat": {
    "default_model": "deepseek-v4-pro",
    "streaming": true,
    "show_tool_calls": true,
    "auto_save": true,
    "confirm_tools": false,
    "max_context_messages": 50,
    "auto_cleanup_days": 90
  },
  "forge": {
    "hermes_profile": "default",
    "agent_model": "deepseek-v4-flash",
    "eval_model": "deepseek-v4-pro",
    "teacher_model": "deepseek-v4-pro",
    "max_concurrent_agents": 4,
    "agent_timeout_minutes": 30,
    "caveman_ultra": true,
    "auto_evaluate": true,
    "save_failed": false
  },
  "advanced": {
    "start_with_windows": false,
    "auto_start_forge": false,
    "minimize_to_tray": true,
    "notifications": true,
    "log_level": "INFO",
    "log_path": "C:/Users/Pontus/.hermes/logs"
  }
}
```

## Design Principles

| Principle | Meaning |
|-----------|---------|
| **App = Mission Control** | The dashboard is the entire program — no separate service |
| **One button for everything** | Start, pause, stop StydeForge from one place |
| **Provider-agnostic** | Switch model with one click — DeepSeek, OpenAI, custom |
| **Chat is an agent** | Not just Q&A — it reads/writes/edits files |
| **Dark and compact** | Terminal aesthetic, nothing unnecessary |
| **Portable** | Single .exe — no dependencies, no installation |

FILE: ./Dashboard_Phase0/00_Overview/Dashboard_Vision.md

# Dashboard Vision & Goals

**StydeForge Dashboard — Mission Control**
**Phase 0 Design Document**

---

## 1. What is StydeForge Dashboard?

StydeForge Dashboard is **the entire program** — not a separate webpage monitoring something else. It is the `StydeForge.exe` desktop application the user interacts with.

Three core functions in a single window:
- **Monitor** — view all agents, benchmarks, system health
- **Control** — start, pause, stop the Forge system
- **Chat** — a full agent that reads/writes files, runs commands, uses skills

---

## 2. Why?

**Today's problem (without Dashboard):**
- Agent monitoring requires terminal commands (`hermes process list`, `hermes cronjob list`)
- No overview of performance and cost over time
- Start/stop done manually via CLI
- No unified place to interact with the system
- Switching models = digging through config files

**Solution:**
A single .exe. Double-click. Everything is there.

---

## 3. Goals

### 3.1 Primary Goals (MVP — Phase 1)

| Goal | Description | Success Criterion |
|------|-------------|-------------------|
| **Agent Monitoring** | See all active/done agents in real-time | List updates within 2s of status change |
| **System Control** | Start/pause/stop Forge from one button | One click = entire pipeline stops |
| **Chat with Tools** | Chat with an AI agent that reads/writes files | Chat can edit a file on disk |
| **Model Switching** | Switch AI model in chat via dropdown | DeepSeek → OpenAI = one click |

### 3.2 Secondary Goals (Phase 2+)

| Goal | Description |
|------|-------------|
| **Benchmark View** | See performance over time — tokens/s, cost, eval results |
| **Custom Providers** | Connect custom LLM via REST endpoint |
| **Local Models** | Support Ollama, llama.cpp — run locally |
| **System Health** | CPU/GPU/RAM/Disk — live |
| **System Tray** | Minimize to tray, notifications for key events |
| **Auto Update** | App updates itself |

---

## 4. Non-Goals (what the Dashboard is NOT)

- **Not an IDE** — no code editor, no project management
- **Not a model trainer** — no fine-tuning, no dataset management
- **Not a web server** — runs locally, no remote access (MVP)
- **Not a terminal replacement** — advanced debugging still done in CLI

---

## 5. User Flow

```
1. Double-click StydeForge.exe
        │
2. Dashboard opens with 3 panels
        │
   ┌────┴────┬────────────┬────────────┐
   │ AGENTS  │ BENCHMARKS │    CHAT    │
   │ (list)  │  (graphs)  │ (full agent│
   └─────────┴────────────┴────────────┘
        │
3. Top bar: [▶ Start] [⏸ Pause] [⏹ Stop] [⚙ Settings]
        │
4. Chat always available — right/bottom panel
   • "read D:/config.yaml and optimize it"
   • Agent reads file, analyzes, writes back
   • "skill:code-review on D:/project/"
   • Agent runs code-review with that skill
```

---

## 6. Target Audience

**Primary:** Pontus (developer, AI engineer)
- Wants control over his agent ecosystem
- Frequently switches models (DeepSeek, OpenAI, local)
- Heavy skill usage
- Wants visibility without digging through logs

**Secondary:** Other developers running Hermes/StydeForge
- Same needs but with their own providers and skills

---

## 7. Success Metrics

| Metric | Target |
|--------|--------|
| Time from double-click to functional dashboard | < 3 seconds |
| Time to switch model in chat | < 5 seconds (select + verify) |
| Steps to stop Forge | 1 click |
| Chat response time (first token) | < 2 seconds |
| Memory usage (idle) | < 150 MB |
| Install size (.exe) | < 80 MB |

---

**Status:** Phase 0 — Design

# Lifecycle Management

**StydeForge Dashboard — Mission Control**
**Phase 0 Design Document**

---

## 1. Overview

The Dashboard is the master controller for the entire StydeForge system. Three states:

```
         ┌──────────────┐
    ┌───→│  STOPPED     │←───┐
    │    └──────┬───────┘    │
    │           │ [Start]    │ [Stop]
    │           ▼            │
    │    ┌──────────────┐    │
    │    │  RUNNING     │────┘
    │    └──────┬───────┘
    │           │ [Pause]
    │           ▼
    │    ┌──────────────┐
    └────│  PAUSED      │
         └──────────────┘
              │ [Start] = Resume
```

---

## 2. State: STOPPED

**UI indicator:** Red status dot + "StydeForge: Inactive"

| Property | Value |
|----------|-------|
| Hermes processes | No Forge processes running |
| Cron jobs | Paused |
| Agent panel | Shows "No agents active" |
| System resources | Dashboard uses minimal CPU/RAM |
| On exit | Prompt whether to start Forge |

---

## 3. State: RUNNING

**UI indicator:** Green status dot + "StydeForge: Running — 3 agents active"

**Startup sequence:**

```
Dashboard [▶ Start]
     │
     ├─→ 1. Validate config
     │      └─ Check all providers have API keys
     │
     ├─→ 2. Start Hermes Forge loop
     │      └─ Spawn as child process: hermes forge start
     │
     ├─→ 3. Start cron jobs
     │      └─ If auto-start of specific jobs is configured
     │
     └─→ 4. Begin polling agent status
            └─ Every 2 seconds: hermes process list
```

**Child process management:**
- Hermes runs as child process under Dashboard
- Dashboard owns the process lifecycle
- If Dashboard crashes → Hermes gets graceful shutdown
- If Hermes crashes → Dashboard shows error, offers restart

---

## 4. State: PAUSED

**UI indicator:** Yellow status dot + "StydeForge: Paused"

| Component | Action |
|-----------|--------|
| Agent spawning | No new agents started |
| Active agents | Allowed to finish current task |
| Cron jobs | Temporarily disabled (set to pause mode) |
| Eval pipeline | Paused after current evaluation |
| Dashboard UI | Continues updating, shows paused status |

**Resume:** Click [▶ Start] → everything resumes where it was.

---

## 5. Stop Sequence (Graceful Shutdown)

```
Dashboard [⏹ Stop]
     │
     ├─→ 1. Show confirmation dialog
     │      "Stop StydeForge? 3 agents currently running."
     │      [Stop Anyway] [Wait Until Done] [Cancel]
     │
     ├─→ 2. Signal stop to Forge loop
     │      └─ Let current agents finish (timeout: 30s)
     │
     ├─→ 3. Save checkpoints
     │      └─ All active agents save their state
     │
     ├─→ 4. Stop cron jobs
     │      └─ Set status=paused on all active cron jobs
     │
     ├─→ 5. Kill Hermes process
     │      └─ SIGTERM → wait 5s → SIGKILL
     │
     └─→ 6. Update UI
            └─ Red dot, "StydeForge: Inactive"
```

---

## 6. Edge Cases

| Scenario | Behavior |
|----------|----------|
| User closes window (✕) | If Forge running: minimize to tray (default) or prompt |
| User closes via tray | Close fully (if Forge not running) or prompt |
| Windows shutdown/reboot | Dashboard captures WM_QUERYENDSESSION → graceful shutdown |
| Power loss / force kill | Next start: "Forge shut down unexpectedly. Restore?" → run recovery |
| Double-launch of Dashboard | Second instance detects first → focus existing window → exit |

---

## 7. Auto-Start

Optional (⚙ settings):
- Start Dashboard with Windows
- Auto-start Forge when Dashboard opens
- Start minimized to system tray

---

**Status:** Phase 0 — Design

========================================================================
FILE: ./Dashboard_Phase0/01_Application_Shell/Process_Control.md
========================================================================

# Process Control

**StydeForge Dashboard — Mission Control**
**Phase 0 Design Document**

---

## 1. Overview

The Dashboard manages Hermes as a child process via Tauri's Rust backend:

```
┌─────────────────────────────────┐
│   Dashboard (Tauri Rust Shell)  │
│                                 │
│   spawn("hermes", ["forge",     │
│          "start"])              │
│         │                       │
│         ▼                       │
│   ┌─────────────────────┐       │
│   │ Child Process       │       │
│   │ hermes forge start  │       │
│   │                     │       │
│   │ stdout/stderr pipes │       │
│   └─────────┬───────────┘       │
│             │                   │
│   ┌─────────┴───────────┐       │
│   │ Process Manager     │       │
│   │ • Monitor stdout    │       │
│   │ • Track PID         │       │
│   │ • Handle crashes    │       │
│   │ • Signal (SIGTERM)  │       │
│   └─────────────────────┘       │
└─────────────────────────────────┘
```

---

## 2. Process Spawning

### 2.1 Hermes Forge Loop

```rust
// Pseudocode — Tauri Rust backend
let hermes_process = Command::new("hermes")
    .args(["forge", "start"])
    .env("HERMES_PROFILE", "default")
    .stdout(Stdio::piped())
    .stderr(Stdio::piped())
    .spawn()?;

// Save PID for later control
state.hermes_pid = hermes_process.id();
```

### 2.2 Ad-hoc Hermes Commands

Dashboard also runs short-lived Hermes commands for data polling:

```rust
// Poll agent status — runs and returns immediately
let output = Command::new("hermes")
    .args(["process", "list", "--json"])
    .output()?;

let agents: Vec<Agent> = serde_json::from_str(&output.stdout)?;
```

---

## 3. Process Monitoring

Dashboard monitors the Hermes process continuously:

| Event | Detection | Action |
|-------|-----------|--------|
| Process crashes | `WaitForSingleObject` on process handle | Show error, offer restart |
| Process hangs | No stdout for 60s | Warning in UI, offer force kill |
| High CPU | >80% for 30s | Warning: "Hermes using high CPU" |
| High memory | >4GB | Warning: "Hermes using high memory" |

---

## 4. Communication with Hermes

### 4.1 stdout/stderr — Real-time Log

Hermes stdout and stderr pipes are read continuously:
- Each line parsed (JSON-lines format from Hermes logging)
- Relevant data pushed to UI (status updates, errors)
- Raw logs saved to disk for debugging

### 4.2 Signal Handling

| Signal | Usage |
|--------|-------|
| SIGTERM | Graceful stop — Hermes finishes active iteration |
| SIGINT | Pause — Hermes pauses after current step |
| SIGKILL | Force kill (last resort, after timeout) |

---

## 5. Cron Job Management

Dashboard controls Hermes cron jobs:

| Action | Hermes Command |
|--------|---------------|
| List all jobs | `hermes cronjob list --json` |
| Start a job | `hermes cronjob resume <job_id>` |
| Pause a job | `hermes cronjob pause <job_id>` |
| Run a job manually | `hermes cronjob run <job_id>` |
| Remove a job | `hermes cronjob remove <job_id>` |

---

## 6. Error Recovery

```
Process crash detected
        │
        ▼
┌─────────────────────┐
│ 1. Log the crash    │
│    (save last 100   │
│     lines of stderr) │
└────────┬────────────┘
         │
         ▼
┌─────────────────────┐
│ 2. Show dialog      │
│ "Hermes crashed.    │
│  Options:           │
│  [Restart]          │
│  [View Log]         │
│  [Close Dashboard]" │
└────────┬────────────┘
         │
         ▼
┌─────────────────────┐
│ 3. If restart:      │
│    • Load latest    │
│      checkpoint     │
│    • Restore agents │
│    • Restart        │
│      Forge loop     │
└─────────────────────┘
```

---

## 7. Process Safety

| Rule | Reason |
|------|--------|
| Only one Forge process at a time | Avoid race conditions |
| Dashboard owns the process | If Dashboard dies → Hermes dies (no zombies) |
| 30s timeout on shutdown | Prevent shutdown from hanging |
| Log all process events | Full traceability for debugging |

---

**Status:** Phase 0 — Design

========================================================================

# System Tray Integration

**StydeForge Dashboard — Mission Control**
**Phase 0 Design Document**

---

## 1. Overview

The Dashboard minimizes to system tray instead of closing entirely — so Forge can keep running in the background.

```
Windows System Tray (taskbar, right side)
┌──────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  ▲  🌐  🔊  [S]  15:34              │
│              ↑                          │
│         StydeForge icon                 │
└──────────────────────────────────────────┘

Right-click icon:
┌────────────────────┐
│ Open Dashboard     │
│ ─────────────      │
│ Status: ● Running  │
│ Agents: 3 active   │
│ Tokens: 12.4K      │
│ ─────────────      │
│ ▶ Start Forge      │
│ ⏸ Pause Forge     │
│ ⏹ Stop Forge      │
│ ─────────────      │
│ ⚙ Settings        │
│ ─────────────      │
│ Exit               │
└────────────────────┘
```

---

## 2. Tray Icon

| Property | Description |
|----------|-------------|
| Icon | Stylized "S" (StydeForge logo) — 16×16 and 32×32 px |
| Color (active) | Green — Forge running |
| Color (paused) | Yellow — Forge paused |
| Color (inactive) | Gray — Forge stopped |
| Color (error) | Red — Forge crashed or errored |

---

## 3. Minimize Behavior

| Action | Result |
|--------|--------|
| Click ✕ (close button) | Minimize to tray (if Forge running) |
| Click ✕ (Forge not active) | Prompt: "Close or minimize?" |
| Double-click tray icon | Open/restore Dashboard window |
| Right-click → Open Dashboard | Restore window, focus |
| Windows+D (show desktop) | Dashboard minimizes normally |
| Alt+Tab | Dashboard visible in Alt+Tab list |

---

## 4. Notifications

Dashboard sends Windows notifications for key events:

| Event | Notification |
|-------|-------------|
| Agent completed (score ≥80) | "✅ Agent 'code-reviewer v3' done! Score: 87/100" |
| Agent completed (score <80) | "⚠ Agent 'sql-helper' scored 62/100 — below quality gate" |
| Forge crashed | "🔴 StydeForge crashed. Click to view log." |
| High resource usage | "⚠ CPU 92% for 30s — may impact performance" |
| Checkpoint saved | "💾 Checkpoint saved: 2026-06-25 15:42" |
| New version available | "🔄 StydeForge v1.1 available! Click to update." |

---

## 5. Notification Interaction

| Click on notification | Result |
|----------------------|--------|
| Agent notification | Open Dashboard → focus agent detail view |
| Crash notification | Open Dashboard → show error log |
| Update notification | Start update process |

---

## 6. Configuration

```json
{
  "tray": {
    "minimize_to_tray": true,
    "show_notifications": true,
    "notification_events": [
      "agent_completed",
      "agent_failed",
      "forge_crashed",
      "update_available"
    ],
    "start_minimized": false
  }
}
```

| Setting | Default | Description |
|---------|---------|-------------|
| `minimize_to_tray` | true | Close = minimize to tray |
| `show_notifications` | true | Show Windows notifications |
| `notification_events` | ["agent_completed", "agent_failed", "forge_crashed", "update_available"] | Events that trigger notifications |
| `start_minimized` | false | Start Dashboard minimized on Windows startup |

---

## 7. Edge Cases

| Scenario | Behavior |
|----------|----------|
| Dashboard starts while Forge already running (from previous session) | Detect existing process, attach to it, don't prompt |
| Windows Explorer crashes/restarts | Tray icon auto-recreated |
| User "closes" via tray while Forge running | Prompt: "Forge is running. [Stop Forge + Exit] [Minimize] [Cancel]" |
| Tray icon not visible (Windows hides it) | Use system "show all icons"; Dashboard shows instruction on first run |

---

**Status:** Phase 0 — Design

# Window Management

**StydeForge Dashboard — Mission Control**
**Phase 0 Design Document**

---

## 1. Window Behavior

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ StydeForge — Mission Control                          ─ □ ✕│
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ [▶ Start] [⏸ Pause] [⏹ Stop] [⚙ Settings]                │
├──────────────────┬──────────────────────┬───────────────────┤
│                  │                      │                   │
│   AGENT PANEL    │   BENCHMARK PANEL    │   CHAT PANEL      │
│   (30%)          │   (35%)              │   (35%)           │
│                  │                      │                   │
│                  │                      │                   │
│                  │                      │                   │
│                  │                      │                   │
├──────────────────┴──────────────────────┴───────────────────┤
│ Status: ● Forge Running | 3 agents active | 12.4K tokens   │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

---

## 2. Specifications

| Property | Value | Note |
|----------|-------|------|
| Default size | 1400×900 px | Comfortably fits all 3 panels |
| Minimum size | 900×600 px | Panels collapse to tabs below 1100px |
| Maximized | Fullscreen with margins | Optimized for 1080p and 1440p |
| Position | Remembers last position | Saved in config |
| Always on top | Toggle (⚙ settings) | For "mission control" feel |
| Title bar | Custom dark title bar | Not Windows default |
| Rounded corners | 8px border-radius | Modern feel |

---

## 3. Panel Layout

### 3.1 Standard Layout (≥1400px width)

```
┌──────────┬───────────────┬───────────────┐
│ AGENTS   │ BENCHMARKS    │ CHAT          │
│          │               │               │
│ 30%      │ 35%           │ 35%           │
│          │               │               │
│ scroll   │ scroll        │ scroll        │
└──────────┴───────────────┴───────────────┘
```

### 3.2 Compact Layout (900-1399px)

```
┌─────────────────┬──────────────────────┐
│ AGENTS (40%)    │ CHAT (60%)           │
│                 │                      │
│ BENCHMARKS      │                      │
│ (hidden — tab   │                      │
│  at top)        │                      │
└─────────────────┴──────────────────────┘
```

### 3.3 Minimal Layout (<900px)

```
┌────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ [Agents] [Benchmarks] [Chat]  ← tabs  │
├────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                        │
│          Active panel                  │
│                                        │
└────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

---

## 4. Draggable Panels

All panel borders are **draggable** (resize handles):
- Cursor changes to ↔ at panel boundary
- Minimum panel width: 200px
- Layout saved in localStorage, restored on next launch
- Double-click panel boundary → reset to default proportions

---

## 5. Keyboard Shortcuts

| Shortcut | Function |
|----------|----------|
| `Ctrl+1` | Focus Agent panel |
| `Ctrl+2` | Focus Benchmark panel |
| `Ctrl+3` | Focus Chat panel |
| `Ctrl+Shift+S` | Start Forge |
| `Ctrl+Shift+P` | Pause Forge |
| `Ctrl+Shift+X` | Stop Forge |
| `Ctrl+,` | Open Settings |
| `Ctrl+K` | Focus chat input |
| `Escape` | Blur/unfocus input field |

---

## 6. Multi-Monitor

| Scenario | Behavior |
|----------|----------|
| Primary screen (1080p) | Standard layout, maximized |
| Secondary screen (1440p/4K) | Move window = keep layout, scale up |
| 3+ screens | Remember position per screen configuration |

---

## 7. Window State

Window state saved in config:
```json
{
  "window": {
    "x": 100,
    "y": 50,
    "width": 1400,
    "height": 900,
    "maximized": false,
    "always_on_top": false,
    "panels": {
      "agents_width": 0.30,
      "benchmarks_width": 0.35
    }
  }
}
```

# Component Library

**StydeForge Dashboard — Mission Control**
**Phase 0 Design Document**

---

## 1. Overview

All reusable UI components. Built as Web Components or vanilla JS — no frameworks. Each component has HTML structure, CSS, and JS behavior defined.

---

## 2. Component Catalog

### 2.1 `sf-button`

```html
<sf-button variant="primary" icon="▶">
  Start Forge
</sf-button>
```

| Attribute | Values | Description |
|-----------|--------|-------------|
| `variant` | `primary`, `secondary`, `danger`, `ghost` | Visual style |
| `size` | `sm`, `md`, `lg` | Size (default: md) |
| `icon` | Any emoji/unicode | Icon before text |
| `disabled` | boolean | Inactive button |

### 2.2 `sf-panel`

```html
<sf-panel title="Agents" icon="📡" collapsible pinned>
  <!-- panel content -->
</sf-panel>
```

| Attribute | Values | Description |
|-----------|--------|-------------|
| `title` | string | Panel header text |
| `icon` | string | Panel icon |
| `collapsible` | boolean | Can be collapsed |
| `pinned` | boolean | Pinned (can't be closed) |

### 2.3 `sf-tabs`

```html
<sf-tabs>
  <sf-tab label="Agents" icon="📡" active>
    <!-- content -->
  </sf-tab>
  <sf-tab label="Benchmarks" icon="📊">
    <!-- content -->
  </sf-tab>
</sf-tabs>
```

### 2.4 `sf-status-bar`

```html
<sf-status-bar>
  <sf-status-item icon="●" value="Running" />
  <sf-status-item label="Agents" value="3" />
  <sf-status-item label="Tokens" value="12.4K" />
  <sf-status-item label="Cost" value="$0.037" />
</sf-status-bar>
```

### 2.5 `sf-agent-card`

```html
<sf-agent-card
  name="code-reviewer-v3"
  model="deepseek-v4-flash"
  status="running"
  score="87"
  tokens="4.2K"
  cost="$0.012"
  time="2m 34s">
</sf-agent-card>
```

Visual design:
```
┌─────────────────────────────────────┐
│ ● code-reviewer-v3         87/100  │
│   deepseek-v4-flash · 2m 34s       │
│   4.2K tokens · $0.012              │
│ ████████████████████░░ 87%  ⚡45t/s│
└─────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 2.6 `sf-chart`

```html
<sf-chart type="line" data="..." width="100%" height="200px">
</sf-chart>
```

| Attribute | Values | Description |
|-----------|--------|-------------|
| `type` | `line`, `bar`, `gauge`, `sparkline` | Chart type |
| `data` | JSON | Data points |
| `width` | CSS value | Width |
| `height` | CSS value | Height |
| `dark` | boolean | Always true in our case |

### 2.7 `sf-log-viewer`

```html
<sf-log-viewer lines="100" filter="ERROR" auto-scroll>
  log text...
</sf-log-viewer>
```

Virtual scrolling for performance with large logs.

### 2.8 `sf-modal`

```html
<sf-modal title="Stop Forge?" open>
  <p>3 agents are still running.</p>
  <sf-button variant="danger">Stop Anyway</sf-button>
  <sf-button variant="secondary">Cancel</sf-button>
</sf-modal>
```

### 2.9 `sf-toast`

```html
<sf-toast type="success" message="Agent completed!" duration="5000">
</sf-toast>
```

Floats in from bottom-right, auto-dismiss.

---

## 3. Chat-Specific Components

### 3.1 `sf-chat-message`

```html
<sf-chat-message role="user" timestamp="15:42">
  optimize my config
</sf-chat-message>

<sf-chat-message role="assistant" model="deepseek-v4-pro" tokens="342" time="1.2s">
  I've read your config.yaml. Here's my analysis...
</sf-chat-message>
```

### 3.2 `sf-chat-input`

```html
<sf-chat-input
  placeholder="Ask anything... /skill:name for skills"
  model-selector
  provider="deepseek"
  model="deepseek-v4-pro">
</sf-chat-input>
```

### 3.3 `sf-tool-call` (embedded in chat)

```html
<sf-tool-call tool="read_file" status="running">
  Reading D:/config.yaml...
</sf-tool-call>

<sf-tool-call tool="read_file" status="done" result="..." time="0.3s">
  Read 42 lines from config.yaml
</sf-tool-call>
```

---

## 4. Provider Components

### 4.1 `sf-provider-card`

```html
<sf-provider-card
  name="DeepSeek"
  models="deepseek-v4-pro, deepseek-v4-flash"
  status="connected"
  latency="120ms">
</sf-provider-card>
```

### 4.2 `sf-provider-form`

```html
<sf-provider-form mode="add">
  <!-- Form to add new provider -->
  <sf-input label="Provider Name" />
  <sf-input label="API Base URL" />
  <sf-input label="API Key" type="password" />
  <sf-button variant="primary">Test Connection</sf-button>
</sf-provider-form>
```

---

## 5. Component States

Every component has defined states:

| State | CSS Class | Example |
|-------|-----------|---------|
| Default | — | Normal state |
| Hover | `.hover` | Mouse over |
| Active | `.active` | Clicked |
| Focus | `.focus` | Keyboard focus |
| Disabled | `.disabled` | Inactive |
| Loading | `.loading` | Shows spinner |
| Error | `.error` | Error state |
| Empty | `.empty` | No data |

---

## 6. Implementation

All components implemented as **Web Components** (Custom Elements v1):

```javascript
class SfButton extends HTMLElement {
  constructor() {
    super();
    this.attachShadow({ mode: 'open' });
  }

  connectedCallback() {
    this.render();
  }

  static get observedAttributes() {
    return ['variant', 'size', 'disabled'];
  }

  render() {
    this.shadowRoot.innerHTML = `
      <style>/* scoped CSS */</style>
      <button class="sf-button ${this.getAttribute('variant')}">
        <slot></slot>
      </button>
    `;
  }
}

customElements.define('sf-button', SfButton);
```

**Benefits:**
- No frameworks — zero dependencies
- Scoped CSS — no style collisions
- Native web standard — works in all WebView environments
- Easy to test — each component isolated

# Design System

**StydeForge Dashboard — Mission Control**
**Phase 0 Design Document**

---

## 1. Design Philosophy

**"Terminal chic"** — dark, compact, functional. Nothing unnecessary.

Inspiration:
- VS Code (dark theme, panel layout)
- Linear (clean typography, subtle animations)
- htop/btm (compact data display)
- Cyberpunk 2077 UI (neon accents, glowing elements)

---

## 2. Color Palette

### 2.1 Primary Palette

| Name | Hex | Usage |
|------|-----|-------|
| **Background** | `#0d0d1a` | App background, main color |
| **Surface** | `#1a1a2e` | Panel background, cards |
| **Surface 2** | `#16213e` | Hover, alternating rows |
| **Border** | `#2a2a4a` | Panel borders, input borders |
| **Text Primary** | `#e0e0e0` | Main text |
| **Text Secondary** | `#8892b0` | Secondary text, labels |
| **Text Muted** | `#4a5568` | Placeholder, inactive text |

### 2.2 Accent Colors

| Name | Hex | Usage |
|------|-----|-------|
| **Primary** | `#6366f1` | Buttons, links, active tab |
| **Primary Hover** | `#818cf8` | Hover on primary elements |
| **Success** | `#10b981` | Done status, positive values |
| **Warning** | `#f59e0b` | Paused, warnings |
| **Danger** | `#ef4444` | Error, stopped, critical |
| **Info** | `#3b82f6` | Information, neutral status |

### 2.3 Status Dots

| Status | Color | Glow |
|--------|-------|------|
| Running | `#10b981` | `box-shadow: 0 0 8px #10b981` |
| Paused | `#f59e0b` | `box-shadow: 0 0 8px #f59e0b` |
| Stopped | `#4a5568` | No glow |
| Error | `#ef4444` | `box-shadow: 0 0 8px #ef4444` (pulsing) |

---

## 3. Typography

### 3.1 Font Stack

```css
font-family: 'JetBrains Mono', 'Fira Code', 'Cascadia Code',
             'Consolas', 'Monaco', monospace;
```

| Usage | Font | Size | Weight |
|-------|------|------|--------|
| Title bar | JetBrains Mono | 14px | 600 |
| Panel headers | JetBrains Mono | 12px | 600 (uppercase, letter-spacing 1px) |
| Body text | JetBrains Mono | 13px | 400 |
| Code | JetBrains Mono | 12px | 400 |
| Small labels | JetBrains Mono | 11px | 400 |
| Status bar | JetBrains Mono | 11px | 500 |

### 3.2 Text Styles

| Style | CSS |
|-------|-----|
| Heading | `font-weight: 600; color: #e0e0e0;` |
| Body | `font-weight: 400; color: #c0c0d0; line-height: 1.6;` |
| Code | `background: #1a1a2e; border-radius: 4px; padding: 2px 6px;` |
| Link | `color: #6366f1; text-decoration: none; &:hover { text-decoration: underline; }` |

---

## 4. Components (Design Tokens)

### 4.1 Buttons

```css
/* Primary button */
.btn-primary {
  background: #6366f1;
  color: #ffffff;
  border: none;
  border-radius: 6px;
  padding: 6px 16px;
  font-size: 12px;
  font-weight: 600;
  cursor: pointer;
  transition: background 0.15s;
}
.btn-primary:hover { background: #818cf8; }
.btn-primary:active { background: #4f46e5; }

/* Secondary button */
.btn-secondary {
  background: transparent;
  color: #c0c0d0;
  border: 1px solid #2a2a4a;
}

/* Danger button */
.btn-danger {
  background: #ef4444;
  color: #ffffff;
}
```

### 4.2 Input Fields

```css
.input {
  background: #0d0d1a;
  border: 1px solid #2a2a4a;
  border-radius: 6px;
  color: #e0e0e0;
  padding: 8px 12px;
  font-family: 'JetBrains Mono', monospace;
  font-size: 13px;
}
.input:focus {
  border-color: #6366f1;
  outline: none;
  box-shadow: 0 0 0 2px rgba(99, 102, 241, 0.2);
}
```

### 4.3 Scrollbars

```css
::-webkit-scrollbar { width: 6px; }
::-webkit-scrollbar-track { background: #0d0d1a; }
::-webkit-scrollbar-thumb {
  background: #2a2a4a;
  border-radius: 3px;
}
::-webkit-scrollbar-thumb:hover { background: #3a3a5a; }
```

---

## 5. Animations

| Element | Animation | Duration | Easing |
|---------|-----------|----------|--------|
| Panel resize | `width` transition | 150ms | ease-out |
| Panel tab switch | `opacity` fade | 200ms | ease-in-out |
| Button hover | `background` color | 150ms | ease |
| Status dot (running) | `box-shadow` pulse | 2s | infinite ease-in-out |
| New agent in list | Slide-in from right | 300ms | ease-out |
| Notification popup | Slide-in from bottom | 400ms | ease-out |

---

## 6. Icons

Minimal, consistent icon set (Lucide-icons style):

| Icon | Usage |
|------|-------|
| ▶ | Start |
| ⏸ | Pause |
| ⏹ | Stop |
| ⚙ | Settings |
| ● | Status (colored) |
| 📡 | Agent panel |
| 📊 | Benchmark panel |
| 💬 | Chat panel |
| 🔄 | Refresh / update |
| 📌 | Pin panel |
| ✕ | Close panel / remove |
| ⚡ | Speed / tokens per second |
| 💾 | Checkpoint / save |

---

## 7. Dark Mode Only

The Dashboard is **dark theme only** — no light mode. This is a design decision, not a preference:

| Reason |
|--------|
| Terminal aesthetic — belongs in the dark |
| Reduces code complexity (no theme variables) |
| Better for long sessions (less eye strain) |
| Matches the StydeForge Forge terminal appearance |

---
